\medskip\noindent\textbf{\underline{Reduction $\red_\mathrm{CBIND}$}:}

\medskip\noindent
On input $(pk,c)$,
\begin{enumerate}
  \item Invoke $\env$. On $(\NewSession, sid, P, P', \pw, \text{``initiator''})$ from $\env$, run $P$'s algorithm to compute $(s,T)$, except that $\red_\mathrm{CBIND}$ uses its input $pk$ instead of $(pk,\star) \gets \Gen$. Send $(s,T)$ to $\adv$.
  \item On $(\NewSession, sid, P', P, \pw', \text{``respondent''})$ from $\env$ and $(s^*,T^*)$ from $\adv$, if $\neg(\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) = (s,T))$, abort. Otherwise generate $(c,K') \gets \Encap(pk)$, and compute $SK := \Hkey(K')$ and $\tau' := \Htag(\pw,pk,s,T,c,K')$. Output $SK'$ to $\env$, and send $(c,\tau')$ to $\adv$.
  \item On $(c^*,\tau^*)$ from $\adv$, if $c^* = c$, abort. Otherwise output $c^*$.
\end{enumerate}

The definition of $\red_\text{CBIND}$ ensures that $\Decap(sk,c) = K'$. If $\adv$ sends $c^*$ such that $\Decap(sk,c^*) = K'$, then $\red_\text{CBIND}$ wins the CBIND game. Thus,
\[
\Pr[\Decap(sk,c^*) = K'] \leq \Adv_{\red_\text{CBIND}}^\text{CBIND}.
\]
If $\Decap(sk,c) \neq K'$, i.e., $K \neq K'$, then of course $P'$'s query is not $\Htag(\pw,pk,s,\allowbreak T,K)$. This yields the claim.
\end{proof}

\subsection{The ``Hash $\pw$ and $(s,T)$'' Version}
\label{sec:hash-pw-st}
We now turn to the variant where $pk$ is further removed from $\Htag$ inputs, i.e., $\tau$ is defined as $\Htag(\pw,s,T,K)$. \Cref{tab:game-summary} suggests that the argument under Game 11 in \Cref{sec:games} need to (essentially) change. (Of course, since $c$ is also removed from $\Htag$, the change in \Cref{sec:hash-pw-pk-st} also needs to be made.) Below we repeat Game 11 and make the new argument.

\medskip\noindent\emph{Game 11:} In the case where $\neg(\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) = (s,T) \land c^* = c)$, if there is no $\langle\pw,pk,sk\rangle$ record, set $SK := \bot$ (i.e., replace the {\color{brown}brown} text in \Cref{fig:intermediate-game} with ``$SK := \bot$'').

Game 10 and Game 11 differ only if $\adv$ does not make an $H_2(\pw,T)$ query, but makes an $\Htag(\pw,s,T,K^*)$ query resulting in $\tau^*$, where $K^* = \Decap(sk,c^*)$ for a freshly generated $sk$. We upper-bound this probability via a reduction $\red_\text{UNPRE}$ to the UNPRE property of the KEM scheme:

\medskip\noindent\textbf{\underline{Reduction $\red_\mathrm{UNPRE}$}:}

\medskip\noindent
\begin{enumerate}
  \item Invoke $\env$. On $(\NewSession, sid, P, P', \pw, \text{``initiator''})$ from $\env$, sample $s \gets \{0,1\}^{3n}, T \gets \group$. Send $(s,T)$ to $\adv$.
  \item On $(\NewSession, sid, P', P, \pw', \text{``respondent''})$ from $\env$ and $(s^*,T^*)$ from $\adv$, run $P'$'s algorithm in Game 10 to compute $c$, $SK'$ and $\tau'$. Output $SK'$ to $\env$, and send $(c,\tau')$ to $\adv$.
  \item On $(c^*,\tau^*)$ from $\adv$, if $\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) = (s,T) \land c^* = c$, abort. Otherwise find $\adv$'s $\Htag(\pw,s,T,K^*)$ query resulting in $\tau^*$. If there is none or more than one, abort. Otherwise output $(c^*,K^*)$.
  \item On $\adv$'s $H_2(\pw^*,T)$ query, if $\pw^* = \pw$, abort. Otherwise do what Game 10 specifies.
\end{enumerate}

It is straightforward to see that if the ``bad event'' above happens, then $\red_\mathrm{UNPRE}$ wins its UNPRE game. We have
\[
\Dist_\env^{10,11} \leq \Adv_{\red_\text{UNPRE}}^\text{UNPRE}.
\]

Overall, we conclude that the ``hash $\pw$ and $(s,T)$'' version is secure under the CBIND and UNPRE properties of the KEM scheme.

\paragraph{The ``hash $\pw$, $(s,T)$ and $c$'' version.}
Note that the change in Game 2 (which requires CBIND) and the change in Game 11 (which require UNPRE) are unrelated to each other. Therefore, if we define $\tau$ as $\Htag(\pw,s,T,c,K)$, then only Game 11 needs to change, and the protocol is secure under the UNPRE property of the KEM scheme.

\subsection{The ``Hash $pk$ and $(s,T)$'' Version}
\label{sec:hash-pk-st}
We now consider the variant where $\pw$, but not $pk$, is further removed from $\Htag$ inputs, i.e., $\tau$ is defined as $\Htag(pk,s,T,K)$. \Cref{tab:game-summary} suggests that Games 2 and 13 in \Cref{sec:games} need to (essentially) change. In fact the simulator also needs to change a bit, which we start from.

\subsubsection{Changes to the Simulator}
The only changes to the simulator $\sim$ appear when $\adv$ sends $(c^*,\tau^*)$ to $P$ and $\sim$ needs to extract a password guess $\pw^*$ from it. In the ``hash everything'' version (\Cref{sec:simulator}), $\tau^*$ is computed as $\Htag(\pw^*,pk^*,s,T,c^*,K^*)$, so $\sim$ can extract $\pw^*$ directly from $\adv$'s $\Htag$ queries and \emph{check its consistency with $pk^*,c^*,K^*$} (see the last paragraph of \Cref{sec:sim-intuition}). Here, $\tau^* = \Htag(pk^*,s,T,K^*)$, which prevents $\sim$ from reading off $\pw^*$ from $\adv$'s $\Htag$ queries. However, the inclusion of $pk^*$ still allows $\sim$ to find the corresponding $\langle\pw^*,pk^*,sk^*\rangle$ record, from which $\sim$ can recover $\pw^*$ and check for consistency. Still, there is a negligible chance that there are multiple $\langle\pw^*,pk^*,sk^*\rangle$ records for the same $pk^*$, which we must rule out.

We show the new simulator in \Cref{fig:oeke-sim-hash-pk-st}. (Only the steps after receiving $(c^*,\tau^*)$ are included.)

\begin{figure}[H]
\begin{framed}
\begin{small}
\underline{$P$'s session key}

\medskip
On $(c^*,\tau^*)$ from $\func$, simulate $P$'s output as follows:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item If $(s^*,T^*) = (s,T) \land (c^*,\tau^*) = (c,\tau')$, send $(\NewKey, sid, P', 0^n)$ to $\func$. \quad \textcolor[gray]{0.5}{// $\adv$ is passive}
  \item Otherwise find $\adv$'s {\color{blue}$\Htag(pk^*,s,T,K^*)$} query resulting in $\tau^*$.
      \begin{enumerate}
        \item If there is no such query or more than one such query, send $(\TestPwd, sid, P, \bot)$ and then $(\NewKey, sid, P, 0^n)$ to $\func$.
        \item If there is exactly one such query, retrieve record $\langle\pw^*,pk^*,sk^*\rangle$. {\color{blue}If there is more than one such record, abort.} If there is no such record, send $(\TestPwd, sid, P, \bot)$ and then $(\NewKey, sid, P, 0^n)$ to $\func$.
        \item Compute $K := \Decap(sk^*,c^*)$. If $K^* \neq K$, send $(\TestPwd, sid, P', \bot)$ and then $(\NewKey, sid, P, 0^n)$ to $\func$.
        \item Send $(\TestPwd, sid, P, \pw^*)$ to $\func$.
            \begin{enumerate}
              \item If $\func$ replies with ``wrong guess'', send $(\NewKey, sid, P, 0^n)$ to $\func$.
              \item If $\func$ replies with ``correct guess'', compute $SK := \Hkey(K)$ and send $(\NewKey, sid, P, SK)$ to $\func$.
            \end{enumerate}
      \end{enumerate}
\end{enumerate}
\end{small}
\end{framed}
\caption{UC simulator $\sim$ for the ``hash $pk$ and $(s,T)$'' variant of OEKE. Only the paragraph that needs essential change (shown in {\color{blue}blue}) is included}
\label{fig:oeke-sim-hash-pk-st}
\end{figure}

\subsubsection{Changes in Game Hops}
\label{sec:hash-pk-st-games}
\paragraph{Change in Game 2.}
The following claim replaces \Cref{clm:htag} in the ``hash everything'' version:
\begin{claim}
\label{clm:htag3}
Suppose the CBIND property holds for the KEM scheme. In the case where $\neg(\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) = (s,T) \land c^* = c)$, the probability that $P'$ queries $\Htag(pk,s,T,K)$ is negligible.
\end{claim}
\begin{proof}
$P'$ makes a single $\Htag$ query, on $(pk',s^*,T^*,K')$. If $(s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T)$, then of course $P'$'s query is not $\Htag(pk,s,T,K)$. Now assume $(s^*,T^*) = (s,T)$, which implies $\pw \neq \pw' \lor c^* \neq c$ by the condition of the claim.
\begin{itemize}
    \item If $\pw \neq \pw'$, we have
      \begin{gather*}
      pk = \frac{T}{R} = \frac{T}{H_1(\pw,r)} = \frac{T}{H_1(\pw,s \oplus t)}, \\
      pk' = \frac{T}{R'} = \frac{T}{H_1(\pw',r')} = \frac{T}{H_1(\pw',s \oplus t')}.
      \end{gather*}
      Since $\pw \neq \pw'$, $H_1(\pw,s \oplus t)$ and $H_1(\pw',s \oplus t')$ are independent of each other, so $\Pr[pk = pk'] = \Pr[H_1(\pw,s \oplus t) = H_1(\pw',s \oplus t')] \leq (q_1+1)/|\group|$.
  \item If $\pw = \pw' \land c^* \neq c$, then $\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) = (s,T)$, which implies that $pk = pk'$ by the definition of $pk$ and $pk'$. Then we can show that $\Pr[K = K']$ is negligible, via a reduction $\Adv_{\red_\text{CBIND}}^\text{CBIND}$ similar to that in the proof of \Cref{clm:htag2}. We have $\Pr[K = K'] \leq \Adv_{\red_\text{CBIND}}^\text{CBIND}$.
\end{itemize}

If $pk \neq pk'$ or $K \neq K'$ then of course $P'$'s query is not $\Htag(pk,s,T,K)$. Overall, we have
\[
\Pr[P'\text{ queries }\Htag(pk,s,T,K)] \leq \Adv_{\red_\text{CBIND}}^\text{CBIND} + \frac{q_1+1}{|\group|},
\]
which yields the claim.
\end{proof}
The remaining argument is essentially identical to that in the old Game 2.

\paragraph{Change in Game 13.}
We first state the new Game 13, and then make the argument.

\medskip\noindent\emph{Game 13:} In the case where $\neg(\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) = (s,T) \land (c^*,\tau^*) = (c,\tau'))$, find $\adv$'s $\Htag(pk^*,s,T,K^*)$ query resulting in $\tau^*$. If there is none or more than one, set $SK := \bot$. Otherwise there is a unique such $\Htag(pk^*,s,T,K^*)$ query, and
\begin{itemize}
  \item If there is more than one $\langle\pw^*,pk^*,sk^*\rangle$ record, abort.
  \item If there is no $\langle\pw^*,pk^*,sk^*\rangle$ record, set $SK := \bot$.
  \item If there is a unique $\langle\pw^*,pk^*,sk^*\rangle$ record, but $\pw^* \neq \pw$, also set $SK := \bot$.
  \item If there is a unique $\langle\pw^*,pk^*,sk^*\rangle$ record, and $\pw^* = \pw$, compute $K := \Decap(sk^*,c^*)$. If $K^* = K$ then set $SK := \Hkey(K)$, otherwise set $SK := \bot$.
\end{itemize}

If $\adv$ makes no $\Htag(\star,s,T,\star)$ query resulting in $\tau^*$, then in particular $\adv$ makes no $\Htag(pk,s,T,\star)$ query resulting in $\tau^*$, so both Game 12 and Game 13 set $SK := \bot$. The probability that $\adv$ makes two different $\Htag(\star,s,T,\star)$ queries both resulting in $\tau^*$ is upper-bounded by $\qtag(\qtag-1)/2^{2n+1}$. (This part does not change from the argument under the old Game 13.) Below we assume that $\adv$ makes a unique $\Htag(pk^*,s,T,K^*)$ query resulting in $\tau^*$:
\begin{itemize}
  \item We first upper-bound the probability that there is more than one $\langle\pw^*,pk^*,\allowbreak sk^*\rangle$ record for the same $pk^*$. Note that in each such record, $(pk^*,\star) \gets \Gen$ is freshly generated, so the probability that there is a collision in $pk^*$ is upper-bounded by ${q_2 \choose 2} \cdot p_\text{guess}$ (recall that there is a $\langle\pw^*,pk^*,sk^*\rangle$ record for each $H_2(\pw^*,T)$ query).
  \item If there is no $\langle\pw^*,pk^*,sk^*\rangle$ record, then both Game 12 and Game 13 set $SK := \bot$.
  \item Next, suppose there is a unique $\langle\pw^*,pk^*,sk^*\rangle$ record, but $\pw^* \neq \pw$. If there is no $\langle\pw,pk,sk\rangle$ record, then both Game 12 and Game 13 set $SK := \bot$. If there is a $\langle\pw,pk,sk\rangle$ record, then $(pk,\star) \gets \Gen$ is freshly generated, so $\Pr[pk^* = pk] \leq q_2 \cdot p_\text{guess}$; and if $pk^* \neq pk$, then $\adv$ does not make an $\Htag(\pw,s,T,pk)$ query resulting in $\tau^*$ (because there is only one $\Htag$ query resulting in $\tau^*$, and it is on $pk^*$), so again both Game 12 and Game 13 set $SK := \bot$.
  \item Finally, if there is a unique $\langle\pw^*,pk^*,sk^*\rangle$ record, and $\pw^* = \pw$, then Game 13 just runs $P$'s algorithm in Game 12, so these two games are identical.
\end{itemize}

In sum, we have
\[
\Dist_\env^{12,13} \leq \frac{q_2(q_2+1)}{2}\cdot p_\text{guess} + \frac{\qtag(\qtag-1)}{2^{2n+1}}.
\]

Overall, we conclude that the ``hash $pk$ and $(s,T)$'' version is secure under the CBIND property of the KEM scheme.

\paragraph{The ``hash $pk$, $(s,T)$ and $c$'' version.}
If we define $\tau$ as $\Htag(pk,s,T,c,K)$, then the second bullet of the proof of \Cref{clm:htag3} is not needed, and the protocol can be proven secure without the CBIND property of the KEM scheme (i.e., under the same assumptions as in the ``hash everything'' version).

\subsection{The ``Only Hash $(s,T)$'' Version}
\label{sec:hash-st}

Finally, we consider the variant where both $\pw$ and $pk$ (as well as $c$) are removed from $\Htag$ inputs, i.e., $\tau$ is defined as $\Htag(s,T,K)$. This is \emph{not} merely a combination of what we did while removing $\pw$ and while removing $pk$ (\Cref{sec:hash-pk-st,sec:hash-pw-st}), and requires a new analysis. Again we will start from the changes to the simulator.

\subsubsection{Changes to the Simulator}
When $\pw$ is removed from $\Htag$ inputs in \Cref{sec:hash-pk-st}, the simulator needs to change how it extracts $\adv$'s password guess $\pw^*$: it cannot read off $\pw^*$ from $\adv$'s $\Htag$ queries, and instead needs to read off $pk^*$ and then fetch the $\langle\pw^*,pk^*,sk^*\rangle$ record. Here, neither $\pw^*$ nor $pk^*$ can be read off from $\adv$'s $\Htag$ queries, and a new extraction strategy is needed. $\sim$ can only read off $K^*$, so it has to go over \emph{all} $\langle\pw^*,pk^*,sk^*\rangle$ records and check which one is consistent with $K^*$ and $c^*$. The new simulator is shown in \Cref{fig:oeke-sim-hash-st}.

\begin{figure}[H]
\begin{framed}
\begin{small}
\underline{$P$'s session key}

\medskip
On $(c^*,\tau^*)$ from $\func$, simulate $P$'s output as follows:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item If $(s^*,T^*) = (s,T) \land (c^*,\tau^*) = (c,\tau')$, send $(\NewKey, sid, P', 0^n)$ to $\func$. \quad \textcolor[gray]{0.5}{// $\adv$ is passive}
  \item Otherwise find $\adv$'s {\color{blue}$\Htag(s,T,K^*)$} query resulting in $\tau^*$.
      \begin{enumerate}
        \item If there is no such query or more than one such query, send $(\TestPwd, sid, P, \bot)$ and then $(\NewKey, sid, P, 0^n)$ to $\func$.
        \item If there is exactly one such query, retrieve {\color{blue}all records in the form of $\langle\pw^*,\star,sk^*\rangle$}. {\color{blue}For each such record}, compute $K := \Decap(sk^*,c^*)$ and check if $K^* = K$. {\color{blue}If there is more than one such record, abort.} If there is no such record, send $(\TestPwd, sid, P, \bot)$ and then $(\NewKey, sid, P, 0^n)$ to $\func$.
        \item {\color{blue}If there is exactly one record $\langle\pw^*,\star,sk^*\rangle$ with $K := \Decap(sk^*,c^*) = K^*$}, send $(\TestPwd, sid, P, \pw^*)$ to $\func$.
            \begin{enumerate}
              \item If $\func$ replies with ``wrong guess'', send $(\NewKey, sid, P, 0^n)$ to $\func$.
              \item If $\func$ replies with ``correct guess'', compute $SK := \Hkey(K)$ and send $(\NewKey, sid, P, SK)$ to $\func$.
            \end{enumerate}
      \end{enumerate}
\end{enumerate}
\end{small}
\end{framed}
\caption{UC simulator $\sim$ for the ``only hash $(s,T)$'' variant of OEKE. Only the paragraph that needs essential change (shown in {\color{blue}blue}) is included}
\label{fig:oeke-sim-hash-st}
\end{figure}

\subsubsection{Changes in Game Hops}

\paragraph{Change in Game 2.}
The following claim replaces \Cref{clm:htag} in the ``hash everything'' version:
\begin{claim}
\label{clm:htag4}
Suppose the CBIND and KBIND properties hold for the KEM scheme. In the case where $\neg(\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) = (s,T) \land c^* = c)$, the probability that $P'$ queries $\Htag(s,T,K)$ is negligible.
\end{claim}
\begin{proof}
$P'$ makes a single $\Htag$ query, on $(s^*,T^*,K')$. If $(s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T)$, then of course $P'$'s query is not $\Htag(s,T,K)$. Now assume $(s^*,T^*) = (s,T)$, which implies $\pw \neq \pw' \lor c^* \neq c$ by the condition of the claim.
\begin{itemize}
  \item If $\pw \neq \pw'$, by the proof of \Cref{clm:htag3}, $pk$ and $pk'$ are independent of each other (where $pk$ is honestly generated and $pk'$ is uniformly random). This suggests that we should upper-bound $\Pr[K = K'] = \Pr[\Decap(sk,c^*) = K']$ via a reduction $\red_\text{KBIND}$ to the KBIND property of the KEM scheme:
      \vspace{-6pt} \\ % force \medskip in itemize environment
      \textbf{\underline{Reduction $\red_\mathrm{KBIND}$}:}
      \vspace{6pt} \\
      Sample $j \gets [q_2+1]$ as a guess that the $j$-th $H_2$ query (by either $\adv$ or $P'$) is $H_2(\pw',T)$. \\
      On input $(pk,pk',c,K')$,
      \begin{enumerate}
        \item Invoke $\env$. On $(\NewSession, sid, P, P', \pw, \text{``initiator''})$ from $\env$, run $P$'s algorithm to compute $(s,T)$, except that $\red_\mathrm{KBIND}$ uses its input $pk$ instead of $(pk,\star) \gets \Gen$. Send $(s,T)$ to $\adv$.
        \item On the $j$-th $H_2(\pw^*,T) =: t'$ query (by either $\adv$ or $\red_\mathrm{KBIND}$ itself on behalf of $P'$ --- see step 3 below), compute
            \[
            r' := s \oplus t', \quad R' := T/pk'.
            \]
            ($pk'$ is part of $\red_\mathrm{KBIND}$'s input.) If $H_1(\pw^*,r')$ has already been defined and it is not $R'$, abort. Otherwise program $H_1(\pw^*,r') := R'$. \quad \textcolor[gray]{0.5}{// Similar to how $H_1$ is programmed in the OW reduction in \Cref{sec:games}, Game 6}
        \item On $(\NewSession, sid, P', P, \pw', \text{``respondent''})$ from $\env$ and $(s^*,T^*)$ from $\adv$, if $\neg(\pw \neq \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) = (s,T))$, abort. Otherwise
            \begin{enumerate}
              \item If $\adv$ has not queried $H_2(\pw',T)$, make this query on behalf of $P'$.
              \item Compute $SK' := \Hkey(K')$ and $\tau' := \Htag(s,T,K')$. Output $SK'$ to $\env$, and send $(c,\tau')$ to $\adv$. ($c$ and $K'$ are part of $\red_\mathrm{KBIND}$'s input.)
            \end{enumerate}
        \item On $(c^*,\tau^*)$ from $\adv$, output $c^*$.
      \end{enumerate}
      Assuming $\Decap(sk,c^*) = K'$ and $\red_\text{KBIND}$'s guess of index $j$ is correct, the only difference between Game 1/2 and $\red_\text{KBIND}$'s simulation (until $\adv$ sends $c^*$) is that $\red_\text{KBIND}$ uses its input $pk'$ to program $H_1(\pw',r')$, and then uses its inputs $(c,K') \gets \Encap(pk')$ as the $P'$-to-$P$ message and compute $SK'$ and $\tau'$. Since $(c,K')$ are also computed as $\Encap(pk')$ in Game 1/2, $\red_\text{KBIND}$ simulates Game 1/2 perfectly. Furthermore, $\red_\text{KBIND}$ wins the KBIND game. We have
      \[
      \Pr[K = K' \mid \pw \neq \pw'] \leq (q_2+1)\Adv_{\red_\text{KBIND}}^\text{KBIND}.
      \]
  \item If $\pw = \pw' \land c^* \neq c$, then the argument in the proof of \Cref{clm:htag2} still holds, and $\Pr[K = K' \mid \pw = \pw' \land c^* \neq c] \leq (q_2+1)\Adv_{\red_\text{CBIND}}^\text{CBIND}$.
\end{itemize}

If $K \neq K'$ then of course $P'$'s query is not $\Htag(s,T,K)$. Overall, we have
\[
\Pr[P'\text{ queries }\Htag(s,T,K)] = \Pr[K = K'] \leq (q_2+1)(\Adv_{\red_\text{CBIND}}^\text{CBIND} + \Adv_{\red_\text{KBIND}}^\text{KBIND}),
\]
which yields the claim.
\end{proof}
The remaining argument is essentially identical to that in the old Game 2.

\paragraph{Change in Game 11.}
Game 10 and Game 11 differ only if $\adv$ does not make an $H_2(\pw,T)$ query, but makes an $\Htag(s,T,K^*)$ query resulting in $\tau^*$, where $K^* = \Decap(sk,c^*)$ for a freshly generated $sk$. By a reduction $\red_\text{UNPRE}$ that is essentially identical to the one in \Cref{sec:hash-pw-st}, we have
\[
\Dist_\env^{10,11} \leq \Adv_{\red_\text{UNPRE}}^\text{UNPRE}.
\]

\paragraph{Change in Game 13.}
We first state the new Game 13, and then make the argument.

\medskip\noindent\emph{Game 13:} In the case where $\neg(\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) = (s,T) \land (c^*,\tau^*) = (c,\tau'))$, find $\adv$'s $\Htag(s,T,K^*)$ query resulting in $\tau^*$. If there is none or more than one, set $SK := \bot$. Otherwise there is a unique such $\Htag(s,T,K^*)$ query, and
\begin{itemize}
  \item For each $\langle\pw^*,pk^*,sk^*\rangle$ record, compute $K := \Decap(sk^*,c^*)$ and check if $K^* = K$. If there is more than one such record, abort.
  \item If there is no such $\langle\pw^*,pk^*,sk^*\rangle$ record, set $SK := \bot$.
  \item If there is a unique such $\langle\pw^*,pk^*,sk^*\rangle$ record, but $\pw^* \neq \pw$, also set $SK := \bot$.
  \item If there is a unique such $\langle\pw^*,pk^*,sk^*\rangle$ record, and $\pw^* = \pw$, set $SK := \Hkey(K)$.
\end{itemize}

If $\adv$ makes no $\Htag(s,T,\star)$ query resulting in $\tau^*$, then both Game 12 and Game 13 set $SK := \bot$. The probability that $\adv$ makes two different $\Htag(s,T,\star)$ queries both resulting in $\tau^*$ is upper-bounded by $\qtag(\qtag-1)/2^{2n+1}$. (This part does not change from the argument under the old Game 13.) Below we assume that $\adv$ makes a unique $\Htag(s,T,K^*)$ query resulting in $\tau^*$:
\begin{itemize}
  \item We first upper-bound the probability that there is more than one $\langle\pw^*,pk^*,\allowbreak sk^*\rangle$ record with $\Decap(sk^*,c^*) = K^*$. Note that in each such record, $(pk^*,sk^*) \gets \Gen$ is freshly generated, so a straightforward reduction to the CR property of the KEM scheme, $\red_\text{CR1}$, shows that the probability that the same $c^*$ decapsulates to the same $K^*$ under two freshly generated $sk^*$ is upper-bounded by ${q_2 \choose 2} \cdot \Adv_{\red_\text{CR1}}^\text{CR}$.
  \item If there is no $\langle\pw^*,pk^*,sk^*\rangle$ record with $\Decap(sk^*,c^*) = K^*$, then both Game 12 and Game 13 set $SK := \bot$.
  \item Next, suppose there is a unique $\langle\pw^*,pk^*,sk^*\rangle$ record with $\Decap(sk^*,c^*) = K^*$, but $\pw^* \neq \pw$. If there is no $\langle\pw,pk,sk\rangle$ record, then both Game 12 and Game 13 set $SK := \bot$. If there is a $\langle\pw,pk,sk\rangle$ record, then $(pk,sk) \gets \Gen$ is freshly generated, so a straightforward reduction to the CR property of the KEM scheme, $\red_\text{CR2}$, shows that the probability that the same $c^*$ decapsulates to the same $K^*$ under both $sk$ and $sk^*$ is upper-bounded by $q_2 \cdot \Adv_{\red_\text{CR2}}^\text{CR}$. If this does not happen, then again both Game 12 and Game 13 set $SK := \bot$.
  \item Finally, if there is a unique $\langle\pw^*,pk^*,sk^*\rangle$ record, and $\pw^* = \pw$, then both Game 12 and Game 13 set $SK := \Hkey(K)$.
\end{itemize}

In sum, we have
\[
\Dist_\env^{12,13} \leq \frac{q_2(q_2-1)}{2} \cdot \Adv_{\red_\text{CR1}}^\text{CR} + q_2 \cdot \Adv_{\red_\text{CR2}}^\text{CR} + \frac{\qtag(\qtag-1)}{2^{2n+1}}.
\]

Overall, we conclude that the ``only hash $(s,T)$'' version is secure under the CBIND, UNPRE, KBIND and CR properties of the KEM scheme.

\paragraph{The ``hash $(s,T)$ and $c$'' version.}
If we define $\tau$ as $\Htag(s,T,c,K)$, then the second bullet of \Cref{clm:htag4} is not needed, and the protocol can be proven secure without the CBIND property of the KEM scheme (but we still need UNPRE, KBIND and CR).

\section{Future Directions}
\label{sec:future-work}
While we aim to provide a comprehensive and thorough analysis of all OEKE-2F variants, there are, unfortunately (or perhaps fortunately?), still a number of open questions stemmed from this work. Below we mention four topics for future work.

\paragraph{Minimal assumptions for OEKE-2F.}
We did not prove any results on whether the KEM security properties used in this work are \emph{minimal}, i.e., whether some weaker properties suffice for OEKE-2F security. It appears that the properties in \Cref{sec:kem-standard} are minimal, as the reductions use them in a ``tight'' manner. It remains to be formally proven that the security of OEKE (even the ``hash everything'' version) implies the KEM properties in \Cref{sec:kem-standard}, i.e., any PPT adversary that breaks these properties can be used to build an adversary that breaks the UC-security of OEKE.

On the other hand, with some thoughts one can realize that the KEM properties in \Cref{sec:kem-additional} are \emph{not} minimal, and some weaker properties suffice. Take CBIND as an example: even if an adversary can break CBIND of the underlying KEM scheme, as long as this behavior can be caught by the simulator, the simulation would still go through. Thus, roughly speaking CBIND can be weakened to the following property: for any PPT adversary $\adv$ in the game in \Cref{def:cbind}, there exists a PPT simulator $\sim$ that outputs a bit indicating whether $\adv$ wins with all but negligible accuracy. ($\sim$ does not know the secret key $sk$.) A similar weakening can be done for KBIND. The UNPRE and CR properties appear minimal.

\paragraph{OEKE-2F security in the game-based setting.}
A natural question is whether we could rely on weaker KEM security properties if we only require game-based security for OEKE-2F. The standard game-based security notion for PAKE is the one in \cite{EC:BelPoiRog00} (henceforth BPR). One important difference between the BPR and UC security notions is that BPR does not require forward secrecy. From the discussion in \Cref{sec:kem-standard}, it seems that some mechanisms in the OW and ANO games (e.g., giving the public key $pk$ to the adversary) are designed solely for the purpose of achieving forward secrecy, so some weaker versions of OW-1PCA and ANO-1PCA should suffice for the BPR security of OEKE-2F.

Furthermore, it seems that the CBIND and KBIND properties do not correspond to any ``real'' attack on OEKE-2F (see \Cref{fn:cbind}), and are needed only for the simulation to go through. Therefore, it is possible that they can be removed in game-based security of (any variant of) OEKE-2F.

On the other hand, it is unclear how significant a game-based security analysis of OEKE-2F would be. Forward secrecy is considered a standard property for PAKE nowadays, and the UC notion has superseded the game-based one(s) in general. As such, this direction does not seem to be the most urgent in the analysis of OEKE-2F.

\paragraph{Extension to EKE.}
This entire work is on OEKE only, and one might wonder including/excluding certain items from the hash would make a difference in EKE. Note that EKE does not have the authenticator $\tau'$ to begin with, so the only question is what should be included in $\Hkey$ inputs (that derive the session key $SK$). \cite[Appendix~A.4]{EC:JanRoyXu25} shows that the second protocol message needs to be included and the first protocol message does not. It is not entirely clear whether hashing the password would weaken the security requirements on KEM: from the EKE security proof in \cite{EC:JanRoyXu25} it seems that hashing the password does not help, but a formal analysis of this is open.

\paragraph{Extension to Tempo.}
Finally, we mention the future direction of the most practical significance. The current description and security analysis of the Tempo protocol assume the ``hash everything'' version. Given how similar the security proof for Tempo is to the proof for OEKE-2F, we speculate that the same optimization --- removing certain items from the ROs while relying on mildly stronger security properties of the underlying KEM scheme --- can be made in Tempo, which would further protect the protocol against side-channel attacks.

\bibliographystyle{alpha}
\bibliography{bib.bib}
\newpage
\appendix
\section{Comparison Between Our Simulator and the One in \cite{EPRINT:ArrBarJar25}}
\label{app:comparison}
Our simulator in \Cref{sec:sim} is, by and large, the same as the one in \cite[Fig.5~and~6]{EPRINT:ArrBarJar25}, although we completely rewrite it to improve readability. We first summarize some of the notational differences in \Cref{tab:sim-notations}.
\begin{table}[H]\centering
\begin{tabular}{ |c|c|c|c| }
\hline
 & \makecell{our \\ notation} & \makecell{notation in \\ \cite{EPRINT:ArrBarJar25}} & comment \\
\hline
protocol parties & $P$, $P'$ & $\mathsf{A}$, $\mathsf{B}$ & \makecell{easy to confuse \\ with adversary $\adv$} \\
\hline
simulated $P$-to-$P'$ message & $(s,T)$ & $(\overline{s},\overline{T})$ & \\
\hline
adversarial $P$-to-$P'$ message & $(s^*,T^*)$ & $(s,T)$ & \\
\hline
$\adv$'s guess of $P'$'s password & $(\pw')^*$ & $\pw^*$ & \\
\hline
\makecell{KEM public key corresponding to \\ correct password guess on $P'$} & $pk'$ & $\mathsf{pk}^*$ & \\
\hline
simulated $P'$-to-$P$ message & $(c,\tau')$ & $(c,\mathsf{tag})$ & \\
\hline
adversarial $P'$-to-$P$ message & $(c^*,\tau^*)$ & $(c,\mathsf{tag})$ & \makecell{same $(c,\mathsf{tag})$ \\ for different things} \\
\hline
$\adv$'s guess of $P$'s password & $\pw^*$ & $\pw^*$ & \makecell{same $\pw^*$ \\ for different things} \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\caption{Comparison of notations between our simulator and the one in \cite{EPRINT:ArrBarJar25}}
\label{tab:sim-notations}
\end{table}

The simulator in \cite{EPRINT:ArrBarJar25} has more bookkeeping and aborts more frequently. In particular, we completely remove their record $\mathsf{forwS}$, and when detecting whether an adversarial $P$-to-$P'$ message contains more than one password guess (causing the simulator to abort), we only check the relevant $H_2$ queries, whereas they check \emph{all} $H_2$ queries --- including those that are completely unrelated to the attack in the $P$-to-$P'$ direction. For a more detailed explanation, see the comment after Game 15 in \Cref{sec:games}.

The only (more or less) essential difference lies in the {\color{red}red} text in \Cref{fig:oeke-sim1}: in the case where the adversary makes an incorrect password guess on $P'$, we compute $c$ from a uniformly random KEM public key $pk'$, whereas they compute $c$ from an honestly generated $pk'$. While both methods work, our method simplifies the reduction; this is further explained in the comment after Game 18 in \Cref{sec:games}, item (2).

\section{Security Analyses of Other Versions (II): Removing $(s,T)$ from the Hash}
\label{app:other-variants-2}
\subsection{The ``Hash $\pw$ and $pk$'' Version}
\label{app:hash-pw-pk}
We start from the version where $\tau$ is defined as $\Htag(\pw,pk,K)$, i.e., $(s,T)$ and $c$ are removed from the hash compared with the ``hash everything'' version. This would best be compared with the protocol (and its security proof) in \Cref{sec:hash-pw-st}, where $\tau$ is defined as $\Htag(\pw,pk,s,T,K)$. Removing $(s,T)$ from the hash introduces a new case that the simulator must take into consideration, which we start from.

\subsubsection{Changes to the Simulator}
\label{app:hash-pw-pk-sim}
The new situation emerges when the adversary $\adv$ decrypts the $P$-to-$P'$ message $(s,T)$ to recover $pk := \mathsf{2F}^{\text{-}1}(\pw,(s,T))$, and then re-encrypts the same $pk$ under the same $\pw'$ to get $(s^*,T^*) \gets \mathsf{2F}(\pw,pk)$. Note that unlike IC, \emph{the $\mathsf{2F}$ encryption is randomized}, so $\adv$'s re-encryption likely results in a different $(s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T)$. Then $\adv$ sends $(s^*,T^*)$ to $P'$, and forwards the $P'$-to-$P$ message $(c,\tau')$ without modification. We show this whole process in \Cref{fig:attack-no-st}.

\begin{figure}[H]
\pseudocodeblock{
P(\pw) \< \< \adv \< \< P'(\pw) \\ 
\< \sendmessageright*[1.5cm]{s,T} \< \< \< \\
\< \< pk := \mathsf{2F}^{\text{-}1}(\pw,(s,T)) \< \< \\
\< \< (s^*,T^*) \gets \mathsf{2F}(\pw,pk) \< \< \\
\< \< \<\sendmessageright*[1.5cm]{s^*,T^*} \< \\
\< \sendmessageleft*[1.5cm]{c,\tau'} \< \< \sendmessageleft*[1.5cm]{c,\tau'} \< \< \\
\text{output }SK' \< \< \< \< \text{output }SK'
}
\caption{New ``attack'' on the ``hash $\pw$ and $pk$'' version}
\label{fig:attack-no-st}
\end{figure}

One can intuitively tell that this does not constitute an actual attack, since the only thing $\adv$ achieves is to modify some protocol messages and cause $P$ and $P'$ to output the same session key --- which $\adv$ \emph{cannot} compute.\footnote{If anything, such an $\adv$ is ``dumber'' than an adversary who performs a regular online attack, since $\adv$ who knows the correct password could have learned the two parties' session keys but wastes such an opportunity.} What $\adv$ essentially does is to run the $\mathsf{2F}$ encryption process using a fresh randomness, yielding another $(s^*,T^*)$ which has the same effect on the $P'$ side as the honest $(s,T)$; in this way, $\adv$ is ``effectively'' passive while actually modifying the $P$-to-$P'$ message. (We stress again that this ``attack'' critically relies on $\mathsf{2F}$ being randomized, and does not work anymore if we replace it with an IC. However, all subsequent ``attacks'' --- in the setting where we further remove $\pw$ and/or $pk$ from $\Htag$ inputs --- work even with IC.)

This example vividly demonstrates why removing $(s,T)$ from the hash does not require more properties of the underlying KEM scheme, but complicates the security proof. Since this ``attack'' requires $\adv$ to decrypt and re-encrypt via some RO queries, the simulator can catch $\adv$ doing so (and can extract the password along the way), and no additional properties on the KEM level are needed. Still, this scenario is not covered by the previous simulator, and the simulator has to create a new case dedicated to this specific scenario. In more detail, the scenario in \Cref{fig:attack-no-st} should be simulated as follows: When $\adv$ decrypts $(s,T)$ under $\pw$, the simulator $\sim$ records $\langle\pw,pk,sk\rangle$ (although there might be a large number of such decryption attempts, and $\sim$ does not know which is the ``right'' one at this point). Then when $\adv$ sends $(s^*,T^*)$ to $P'$, $\sim$ extracts the ``right'' $\pw$, which allows $\sim$ to compromise $P'$'s session. Later, when $\adv$ sends $(c^*,\tau')$, $\sim$ can tell that $\adv$ is performing the aforementioned ``attack'', and can use the same $\pw$ to compromise $P$'s session.

\begin{remark}
Looking ahead, all subsequent ``attacks'' follow a similar pattern:
\begin{itemize}
  \item In the first protocol message, $\adv$ decrypts $(s,T)$ and re-encrypts to some other $(s^*,T^*)$, and
  \item In the second protocol message, $\adv$ forwards $\tau'$ (but may or may not modify $c$).
\end{itemize}
If we include $(s,T)$ in $\Htag$ inputs, this will immediately result in $P$ rejecting, since $P$'s check will fail. However, without $(s,T)$ in the hash, we have to take this scenario into account. The difference from what's in this section is that if we additionally remove $\pw$ and/or $pk$ from the hash, then $\adv$ can re-encrypt the same $pk$ under another $\pw'$, and/or re-encrypt another $pk^*$ under the same $\pw$. Hence, \Cref{fig:attack-no-st} is a special case of all subsequent ``attacks''.
\end{remark}

We show the new simulator in \Cref{fig:oeke-sim-hash-pw-pk}. (Only the steps after receiving $(c^*,\tau^*)$ are included.)

\begin{figure}[H]
\begin{framed}
\begin{small}
\underline{$P$'s session key}

\medskip
On $(c^*,\tau^*)$ from $\func$, simulate $P$'s output as follows:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item If $(s^*,T^*) = (s,T) \land (c^*,\tau^*) = (c,\tau')$, send $(\NewKey, sid, P', 0^n)$ to $\func$. \quad \textcolor[gray]{0.5}{// $\adv$ is passive}
  {\color{blue}\item If $(s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T) \land (c^*,\tau^*) = (c,\tau')$, and there has been a $(\TestPwd, sid, P', \pw')$ command to $\func$ resulting in ``correct guess'' (i.e., $\sim$ previously entered step 2(b)(ii) in \Cref{fig:oeke-sim2}), there must be a $pk'$ and an $SK'$ defined at that time. 
      \begin{enumerate}
        \item Retrieve record $\langle\pw',pk,\star\rangle$. If there is no such record, go to step 3. \quad \textcolor[gray]{0.5}{// $\adv$ does not decrypt $pk := \mathsf{2F}^{\text{-}1}(\pw,(s,T))$}
        \item If $pk \neq pk'$, go to step 3. \quad \textcolor[gray]{0.5}{// $\adv$ decrypts $(s,T)$ and gets $pk$, but then re-encrypts $(s^*,T^*) \gets \mathsf{2F}(\pw,pk')$ for another $pk'$}
        \item Send $(\TestPwd, sid, P, \pw')$ to $\func$.
            \begin{enumerate}
              \item If $\func$ replies with ``wrong guess'', send $(\NewKey, sid, P, 0^n)$ to $\func$. \quad \textcolor[gray]{0.5}{// $P$ and $P'$'s passwords are different}
              \item If $\func$ replies with ``correct guess'', send $(\NewKey, sid, P, SK')$ to $\func$.
            \end{enumerate}
      \end{enumerate}
  }
  \item Otherwise find $\adv$'s {\color{blue}$\Htag(\pw^*,pk^*,K^*)$} query resulting in $\tau^*$.
      \begin{enumerate}
        \item If there is no such query or more than one such query, send $(\TestPwd, sid, P, \bot)$ and then $(\NewKey, sid, P, 0^n)$ to $\func$.
        \item If there is exactly one such query, retrieve record $\langle\pw^*,\star,sk^*\rangle$. If there is no such record, send $(\TestPwd, sid, P, \bot)$ and then $(\NewKey, sid, P, 0^n)$ to $\func$.
        \item Compute $K := \Decap(sk^*,c^*)$. If $K^* \neq K$, send $(\TestPwd, sid, P', \bot)$ and then $(\NewKey, sid, P, 0^n)$ to $\func$.
        \item Send $(\TestPwd, sid, P, \pw')$ to $\func$.
            \begin{enumerate}
              \item If $\func$ replies with ``wrong guess'', send $(\NewKey, sid, P, 0^n)$ to $\func$.
              \item If $\func$ replies with ``correct guess'', compute $SK := \Hkey(K)$ and send $(\NewKey, sid, P, SK)$ to $\func$.
            \end{enumerate}
      \end{enumerate}
\end{enumerate}
\end{small}
\end{framed}
\caption{UC simulator $\sim$ for the ``hash $\pw$ and $pk$'' variant of OEKE. Only the paragraph that needs essential change (shown in {\color{blue}blue}) is included}
\label{fig:oeke-sim-hash-pw-pk}
\end{figure}

\begin{remark}
We briefly mention another possible simulation strategy. Referring to \Cref{fig:attack-no-st}, computing $pk := \mathsf{2F}^{\text{-}1}(\pw,(s,T))$ requires $\adv$ to query $H_2(\pw,T)$, at which time the simulator $\sim$ stores $\langle\pw,pk,sk\rangle$. Later when $\sim$ simulates the $P'$-to-$P$ message, it needs to compute $(c,K) \gets \Encap(pk)$ and $\tau' := \Htag(\pw,pk,K)$ (see step 2(b)(ii) of \Cref{fig:oeke-sim1}). Therefore, in \Cref{fig:oeke-sim-hash-pw-pk} we could remove step 2, and instead in step 3 find $\adv$ \emph{{\color{blue}or $\sim$ itself}}'s $\Htag(\pw^*,pk^*,K^*)$ query resulting in $\tau^*$, which will still result in $\sim$ finding $\pw$ and sending $(\TestPwd, sid, P, \allowbreak\pw)$ to $\func$. This is essentially what the simulator in \cite{EC:JanRoyXu25} does, and yields a simpler simulator. We choose to present our simulator in the more complicated way because it explicitly highlights the ``attack'' in \Cref{fig:attack-no-st} and thus provides a clearer comparison with the ``hash everything'' version of the protocol.

The same remark goes for subsequent simulators in this section.
\end{remark}

\subsubsection{Changes in Game Hops}
\label{app:game-hops-hash-pw-pk}
Note that \Cref{clm:htag} in Game 2 does not hold anymore, exactly due to what the adversary can do in \Cref{fig:attack-no-pk} ($P$ does not reject even though $\adv$ is not passive and $\adv$ makes no $\Htag$ query whatsoever). As such, Game 2 needs to change essentially. Since Game 2 is almost at the beginning of the sequence of games, this affects some subsequent games and we need to proceed carefully. The trick is to isolate the specific case of the new ``attack'', i.e., the case that makes \Cref{clm:htag} fail; in this case we need to additionally check $P'$'s $\Htag$ query, whereas in all other cases we can proceed as before. In this way we minimize the affect of the change in Game 2.

We start from describing the new Game 2. Most of the subsequent argument is clerical work verifying that the previous argument still goes through; the parts that need to essentially change are shown in {\color{blue}blue}.

\medskip\noindent\emph{Game 2:} In the case where {\color{blue}$\pw \neq \pw' \lor c^* \neq c$}, find $\adv$'s $\Htag(\pw,pk,K^*)$ query resulting in $\tau^*$. If there is none or more than one, set $SK := \bot$. If there is a unique such query, do the following:
\begin{itemize}
  \item If $K^* = K$, set $SK := \Hkey(K)$ (i.e., there is no change from Game 1).
  \item If $K^* \neq K$, set $SK := \bot$.
\end{itemize}

Furthermore, in the case where $\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T) \land c^* = c$, do the same as above, except that we now find $\adv$ {\color{blue}\emph{or $P'$}}'s $\Htag(\pw,pk,K^*)$ query resulting in $\tau^*$.

{\color{blue}The difference between the new Game 2 and the old one is that we now have two separate cases:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item $\pw \neq \pw' \lor c^* \neq c$;
  \item $\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T) \land c^* = c$.
\end{enumerate}
}
These two cases combined yield $\neg(\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) = (s,T) \land c^* = c)$, which is identical to the case in the old Game 2 (i.e., they cover all situations other than the one addressed in Game 1). In case (1) we proceed as in the old Game 2, whereas {\color{blue}in case (2) we cannot due to the ``attack'' in \Cref{fig:attack-no-st}; instead, in case (2) we need to include $P'$'s $\Htag$ query as if it were $\adv$'s}.
\begin{claim}
\label{clm:htag5}
Suppose the CBIND property holds for the KEM scheme. In case (1) above, the probability that $P'$ queries $\Htag(\pw,pk,K)$ is negligible.
\end{claim}
\begin{proof}
$P'$ makes a single $\Htag$ query, on $(\pw',pk',K')$. If $\pw \neq \pw'$, then of course $P'$'s query is not $\Htag(\pw,pk,K)$. Now assume $\pw = \pw'$. This implies $c^* \neq c$ by the condition of the claim.

We now claim that $pk = pk' \land K = K'$ happens with negligible probability. Suppose $pk = pk'$. Then we can reduce the event $K = K'$ to the CBIND property of the KEM scheme, via a reduction $\Adv_{\red_\text{CBIND}}^\text{CBIND}$ similar to that in the proof of \Cref{clm:htag2}. We have $\Pr[pk = pk' \land K = K'] \leq \Adv_{\red_\text{CBIND}}^\text{CBIND}$.

If $pk \neq pk'$ or $K \neq K'$ then of course $P'$'s query is not $\Htag(\pw,pk,K)$. We have
\[
\Pr[P'\text{ queries }\Htag(\pw,pk,K)] \leq \Adv_{\red_\text{CBIND}}^\text{CBIND},
\]
which yields the claim.
\end{proof}
The remaining argument is essentially identical to that under the old Game 2.

\medskip
For subsequent games, if they only involve case (1) in Game 2 then they do not need to change, since the new Game 2 does not make any change in this case. However, if a game involves case (2) then some changes need to be made, since the new Game 2 additionally checks $P'$'s $\Htag$ queries, which a reduction might not be able to do.

\medskip\noindent\emph{Games 3--4:} These two games deal with the case where $\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) = (s,T)$. This falls into either the case in Game 1 (if $c^* = c$) or case (1) in Game 2 (if $c^* \neq c$); either way, it does not enter case (2) in Game 2, so the reductions still go through: they abort if $\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) = (s,T)$ does not hold, and if $\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) = (s,T)$, they can still simulate the games by checking $\adv$'s $\Htag$ queries. Crucially, the reductions do not need to check $P'$'s $\Htag$ query (which they cannot do), since in this case we have defined Game 2 so that it only checks $\adv$'s $\Htag$ queries.

\medskip\noindent\emph{Game 5:} This game involves a reduction to the UNI-PK property of the KEM scheme. The reduction works essentially because $sk'$ is not used anywhere in the game (so the reduction can embed its challenge as $pk'$ without knowing $sk'$), and this fact still holds even though we need to additionally check $P'$'s $\Htag$ queries in some cases now. So, this reduction still goes through.

\medskip\noindent\emph{Games 6--8:} These three games deal with the case where $\pw \neq \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) = (s,T)$. This falls into case (1) in Game 2, so the reductions in Games 6 and 7 still go through; Game 8 involves a statistical argument which does not need to change either.

\medskip\noindent\emph{Games 9--10:} These two games involve statistical arguments only, and they have nothing to do with whether the games need to check $P'$'s $\Htag$ queries.

\medskip\noindent\emph{Game 11:} This game hop goes through for essentially the same reason as in \Cref{sec:games}. The difference is that now Game 10 and Game 11 differ if $\adv$ does not make an $H_2(\pw,T)$ query, but $\adv$ \emph{{\color{blue}or $P'$}} makes an $\Htag(\pw,pk,K^*)$ query resulting in $\tau^*$. However, $pk$ is freshly generated by $P$, independent of \emph{both} $\adv$ and $P'$'s views. Thus, the distinguishing advantage between Game 10 and Game 11 is still upper-bounded by $p_\text{guess}$.

\medskip\noindent\emph{Game 12:} This game should read as follows now: In the case where $\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) = (s,T) \land c^* = c \land \tau^* \neq \tau'$, do what's in the {\color{blue}$\pw \neq \pw' \lor c^* \neq c$ case (i.e., case (1) in Game 2)}.

This game only involves case (1) in Game 2, i.e., it checks $\adv$'s $\Htag$ queries \emph{but does not check $P'$'s $\Htag$ query}. Therefore, this game hop has nothing to do with what's different in the new Game 2, and the previous argument still goes through.

\medskip\noindent\emph{Game 13:} This game should now extract $\pw^*$ from $\adv$ {\color{blue}\emph{or $P'$}}'s $\Htag$ query, if case (2) in Game 2 happens. For completeness, we include a full description of the game.

In the case where {\color{blue}$\pw \neq \pw' \lor c^* \neq c \lor (\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) = (s,T) \land c^* = c \land \tau^* \neq \tau')$}, find $\adv$'s $\Htag(\pw^*,pk^*,K^*)$ query resulting in $\tau^*$. If there is none or more than one, set $SK := \bot$. Otherwise there is a unique such $\Htag(\pw^*,pk^*,K^*)$ query, and
\begin{itemize}
  \item If $\pw^* \neq \pw$, set $SK := \bot$.
  \item If $\pw^* = \pw$, there is no change from Game 12.
\end{itemize}

Furthermore, in the case where $\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T) \land c^* = c$ (i.e., case (2) in Game 2), do the same as above, except that we now find $\adv$ {\color{blue}\emph{or $P'$}}'s $\Htag(\pw^*,pk^*,K^*)$ query resulting in $\tau^*$.

The previous statistical argument is based on ruling out collisions in $\Htag$. Here we can still rule out such collisions, except that the probability of a collision is $\qtag(\qtag+1)/2$ rather than $\qtag(\qtag-1)/2$ (since we may additionally count the $\Htag$ query by $P'$). The rest of the argument does not change.

\medskip\noindent\emph{Games 14--16:} The statistical arguments for these three games do not need to change.

{\color{blue}
\medskip\noindent\emph{New Game I:} Now that $(\pw')^*$ --- the password guess extracted from $(s^*,T^*)$ --- is defined (in Game 15), we can finally add (part of) what's in step 2 of \Cref{fig:oeke-sim-hash-pw-pk}. Concretely, we change the game as follows:

In the case where $(s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T) \land (\pw')^* = \pw = \pw' \land (c^*,\tau^*) = (c,\tau')$, there is a record $\langle\pw,pk,\star\rangle$, and $pk = pk'$, set $SK := SK'$. If $(\pw')^*$ is undefined, treat it as if $(\pw')^* \neq \pw'$. (In some sense this is the most crucial new game, as it covers the scenario in \Cref{fig:attack-no-st} --- which is why we need to make all these changes to begin with. It also corresponds to step 2(c)(ii) in the simulator in \Cref{fig:oeke-sim-hash-pw-pk}. We will deal with step 2(c)(i) in new Game III later.)

Since $\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T) \land (c^*,\tau^*) = (c,\tau')$, Game 16 finds $\adv$ or $P'$'s $\Htag$ query resulting in $\tau^*$ (see the description of Game 13). $P'$ makes a single query to $\Htag$, on input $(\pw',pk',K')$; and the query result is $\tau' = \tau^*$. Therefore, Game 16 finds this query, and does the following (again see the description of Game 13):
\begin{enumerate}
  \item Check if $\pw' = \pw$, which is indeed the case.
  \item Retrieve the $\langle\pw,pk,sk\rangle$ record (as what Game 11 dictates).
  \item Compute $K := \Decap(sk,c^*)$ and check if $K' = K$. Note that
      \begin{gather*}
      (c,K') \gets \Encap(pk')\text{ on the }P'\text{ side}, \\
      c^* = c, \\
      K = \Decap(sk,c^*)\text{ on the }P\text{ side},
      \end{gather*}
      furthermore $pk = pk'$ (per the condition of the game) and $(pk,sk)$ are an honestly generated KEM public/secret key pair (per step 2 above), so by the correctness of the KEM scheme, the $K' \stackrel{?}{=} K$ check passes except with probability $\varepsilon_\text{correctness}$.
  \item Set $SK := \Hkey(K) (= \Hkey(K') = SK')$.
\end{enumerate}
This entire process in Game 16 eventually results in setting $SK := SK'$ except with probability $\varepsilon_\text{correctness}$, which exactly matches the new game. We have
\[
\Dist_\env^{16,\text{newI}} \leq \varepsilon_\text{correctness}.
\]
}

In case (2) in Game 2, we have to check both $\adv$ and $P'$'s $\Htag$ queries, exactly because of the special scenario in new Game I (i.e., in \Cref{fig:attack-no-st}). Now that this case has been singled out and dealt with, we can remove the check of $P'$'s $\Htag$ queries.

{\color{blue}
\medskip
\noindent\emph{New Game II:} In the case where $\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T) \land c^* = c$ (i.e., case (2) in Game 2), we find $\adv$ \emph{or $P'$}'s $\Htag(\pw^*,pk^*,K^*)$ query resulting in $\tau^*$ --- except that in new Game I's condition, new Game I already shortcuts it to $SK := SK'$ without trying to find any $\Htag$ query. In this game, we do not check $P'$'s $\Htag$ query anymore, and only check $\adv$'s $\Htag$ query.

\begin{claim}
\label{clm:pk-ind}
If $(\pw')^* \neq \pw'$ then $pk$ and $pk'$ are independent of each other. ($pk$ is the item in record $\langle\pw,pk,sk\rangle$.)
\end{claim}
\begin{proof}
We have (in the creation of the record $\langle\pw,pk,sk\rangle$)
\[
pk = \frac{T}{R} = \frac{T}{H_1(\pw,r)} = \frac{T}{H_1(\pw,s \oplus t)} = \frac{T}{H_1(\pw,s \oplus H_2(\pw,T))},
\]
and (in $P'$'s algorithm)
\[
pk' = \frac{T^*}{R'} = \frac{T^*}{H_1(\pw,r')} = \frac{T^*}{H_1(\pw,s^* \oplus t')} = \frac{T^*}{H_1(\pw,s^* \oplus H_2(\pw,T^*))}
\]
(recall $\pw = \pw'$ by the condition of the game). If $\adv$ does not query $H_1(\pw,s^* \oplus H_2(\pw,T^*))$, then of course $pk'$ is independent of $pk$. Now suppose $\adv$ queries $H_1(\pw,s^*\allowbreak\oplus H_2(\pw,T^*))$. Recall that $(\pw')^*$ is defined via types (1) and (2) in Game 15 in \Cref{sec:games}:
\begin{itemize}
  \item If $s^*\oplus H_2(\pw,T^*) = s \oplus H_2(\pw,T)$, then $(\pw')^*$ is set to $\pw$ in type (2);
  \item If the $H_1(\pw,s^*\allowbreak\oplus H_2(\pw,T^*))$ query is made before $\adv$'s $H_2(\pw,T^*)$ query, then $(\pw')^*$ is set to $\pw$ in type (1).
\end{itemize}
Since $(\pw')^* \neq \pw'$, the only possibility is that $\adv$ makes a \emph{fresh} $H_1(\pw,s^*\allowbreak\oplus H_2(\pw,T^*))$ query \emph{after} its $H_2(\pw,T^*)$ query (in particular, after $T^*$ is fixed), which causes $pk'$ to be independent of $pk$.
\end{proof}

Going back to the game, there are the following cases:
\begin{itemize}
  \item If $\tau^* \neq \tau'$, then of course $P'$'s $\Htag$ query does not result in $\tau^*$ (it results in $\tau'$), so we can safely drop $P'$'s $\Htag$ query from the check.
  \item If $\tau^* = \tau'$, but there is no $\langle\pw,pk,\star\rangle$ record, then both new Game I and new Game II outright set $SK := \bot$, regardless of $\Htag$ queries by $\adv$ or $P'$. Thus, the two games are identical.
  \item If $(\pw')^* \neq \pw' \land \tau^* = \tau'$, and there is a record $\langle\pw,pk,\star\rangle$, then $P'$'s $\Htag(\pw',pk',K')$ query results in $\tau^*$, and we need to argue that this query can be dropped from the check.
      \begin{itemize}
        \item If $\adv$ queries $\Htag(\pw',pk',K')$, then new Game II still finds this query, so new Game I and new Game II are identical.
        \item If $\adv$ does not query $\Htag(\pw',pk',K')$, then new Game II sets $SK := \bot$. We argue that new Game I also sets $SK := \bot$ except with negligible probability. New Game I finds $P'$'s $\Htag(\pw',pk',K')$ query, and sets $SK := \bot$ if $pk \neq pk'$. But $pk$ and $pk'$ are independent of each other by \Cref{clm:pk-ind}, so $\Pr[pk = pk'] \leq p_\text{guess}$.
      \end{itemize}
  \item If $(\pw')^* = \pw' \land \tau^* = \tau'$, there is a record $\langle\pw,pk,\star\rangle$, but $pk \neq pk'$, then new Game I finds $P'$'s $\Htag(\pw',pk',K')$ query and then sets $SK := \bot$ because $pk \neq pk'$, and new Game II also sets $SK := \bot$ because it either fails to find $\adv$'s $\Htag(\pw',pk',K')$ query, or it finds such a query but then sets $SK := \bot$ because $pk \neq pk'$. Thus, the two games are identical.
\end{itemize}

The remaining case is that $(\pw')^* = \pw' \land \tau^* = \tau'$, there is a record $\langle\pw,pk,\star\rangle$, and $pk = pk'$. The condition of the game additionally requires $\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T) \land c^* = c$. Combined, we get ``$(s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T) \land (\pw')^* = \pw = \pw' \land (c^*,\tau^*) = (c,\tau')$, there is a record $\langle\pw,pk,\star\rangle$, and $pk = pk'$''. This is exactly the condition in new Game I, in which case we do not make any change in new Game II. Overall, we conclude that
\[
\Dist_\env^{\text{newI},\text{newII}} \leq p_\text{guess}.
\]}

\noindent\emph{Game 17:} Note that after new Game II, we never try to find $P'$'s $\Htag$ query anymore: in some cases we try to find $\adv$'s $\Htag$ query, and in other cases we outright set $SK$ to be a certain value or $\bot$. Therefore, the reduction still goes through (it can simulate the $P$ side honestly).\footnote{New Games I and II --- which drop $P'$'s $\Htag$ query from the check --- have to be inserted before Game 17, since the reduction in Game 17 cannot check $P'$'s $\Htag$ query (the query is $\Htag(\pw',pk',K')$, and the reduction does not know $K'$).}

{\color{blue}
\medskip\noindent\emph{New Game III:}
In the case where $(s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T) \land (\pw')^* = \pw' \neq \pw \land (c^*,\tau^*) = (c,\tau')$, there is a record $\langle\pw,pk,\star\rangle$, and $pk = pk'$, set $SK := \bot$. (This corresponds to step 2(c)(i) in \Cref{fig:oeke-sim-hash-pw-pk}.)

In this case Game 17 tries to find $\adv$'s (unique) $\Htag(\pw^*,pk^*,K^*)$ query resulting in $\tau^*$, and checks if $\pw^* = \pw$ (see Game 13). But $\tau^* = \tau' = \Htag(\pw',pk',K')$, so Game 17 sets $SK := \bot$ because it either fails to find $\adv$'s $\Htag(\pw',pk',K')$ query, or it finds such a query but then sets $SK := \bot$ because $\pw^* = \pw' \neq \pw$. Either way, Game 17 matches new Game III which outright sets $SK := \bot$. We have
\[
\Dist_\env^{17,\text{newIII}} = 0.
\]

\paragraph{Summary.}
We have made the following essential changes to the games:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item In the case where $\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T) \land c^* = c$ (case (2) in Game 2), Game 2 tries to find $P'$'s $\Htag$ query resulting in $\tau^*$ (in addition to $\adv$'s query).
  \item In the case where $(s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T) \land (\pw')^* = \pw = \pw' \land \tau^* = \tau'$, there is a record $\langle\pw,pk,\star\rangle$, and $pk = pk'$, new Game I outright sets $SK := SK'$ (without trying to find any $\Htag$ query by $\adv$ or $P'$).
  \item In the case where $\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T) \land c^* = c$, new Game II drops the check on $P'$'s $\Htag$ query introduced in Game 2 (except in new Game I's condition, where all checks on $\Htag$ queries have already been dropped).
  \item In the case where $(s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T) \land (\pw')^* = \pw' \neq \pw \land \tau^* = \tau'$, there is a record $\langle\pw,pk,\star\rangle$, and $pk = pk'$, new Game III outright sets $SK := \bot$.
\end{enumerate}

Items (1) and (3) introduce the check on $P'$'s $\Htag$ query and then drop it, so there is no net change there. To see the net change, we only need to combine items (2) and (4), which say that in the case where $(s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T) \land (\pw')^* = \pw' \land \tau^* = \tau'$, there is a record $\langle\pw,pk,\star\rangle$, and $pk = pk'$,
\begin{itemize}
  \item If $(\pw')^* = \pw$, then we set $SK := \Hkey(K')$ [item (2)].
  \item If $(\pw')^* \neq \pw$, then we set $SK := \bot$ [item (4)].
\end{itemize}
This exactly matches step 2 of the simulator in \Cref{fig:oeke-sim-hash-pw}, so new Game III is identical to the ideal world.} This completes the proof.

\paragraph{The ``hash $\pw$, $pk$ and $c$'' version.}
If we define $\tau$ as $\Htag(\pw,pk,c,K)$, then \Cref{clm:htag5} unconditionally holds, and the protocol can be proven secure without the CBIND property of the KEM scheme (i.e., under the same assumptions as in the ``hash everything'' version).

\subsection{The ``Hash $\pw$'' Version}
\label{app:hash-pw}
We now consider the variant where $pk$ is further removed from $\Htag$ inputs, i.e., $\tau$ is defined as $\Htag(\pw,K)$. This would best be compared with the protocol (and its security proof) in \Cref{sec:hash-pw-st}, where $\tau$ is defined as $\Htag(\pw,s,T,K)$; as well as the protocol (and its security proof) in \Cref{app:hash-pw-pk}, where $\tau$ is defined as $\Htag(\pw,pk,K)$. As we have seen in \Cref{app:hash-pw-pk}, removing $(s,T)$ from the hash introduces a new ``re-encryption'' case that the simulator must take into consideration. After further removing $pk$, there is a more general ``attack'' we need to take into account, which we start from.

\subsubsection{Changes to the Simulator}
\label{app:hash-pw-sim}
The easiest way to see the new, more general ``attack'' is to work out a concrete version for OEKE based on the Diffie--Hellman KEM, which we show in \Cref{fig:attack-no-pk}.

\begin{figure}[H]
\pseudocodeblock[codesize=\scriptsize]{
P(\pw) \< \< \adv \< \< P'(\pw) \\ 
\< \sendmessageright*[1.5cm]{s,T} \< \< \< \\
\< \< X := \mathsf{2F}^{\text{-}1}(\pw,(s,T)) \< \< \\
\< \< (s^*,T^*) \gets \mathsf{2F}(\pw,X^2) \< \< \\
\< \< \<\sendmessageright*[1.5cm]{s^*,T^*} \< \\
\< \sendmessageleft*[1.5cm]{Y^2,\tau'} \< \< \sendmessageleft*[1.5cm]{Y,\tau'} \< \< \\
\text{output} \< \< \< \< \text{output} \\
\Hkey((Y^2)^x) = \Hkey(g^{2xy}) \< \< \< \< \Hkey((X^2)^y) = \Hkey(g^{2xy})
}
\caption{New ``attack'' on the ``hash $\pw$'' version, using OEKE based on Diffie--Hellman KEM}
\label{fig:attack-no-pk}
\end{figure}

In this ``attack'', the two honest parties' passwords $\pw$ are the same. Assuming $\adv$ knows it, it can decrypt $P$'s message to recover $X = g^x$, and then re-encrypt $X^2$ under the same $\pw$; this causes $P'$ to output $SK' = \Hkey(g^{2xy})$ and send $(Y = g^y, \tau' = \Htag(\pw,g^{2xy}))$. Then $\adv$ sends $(Y^2,\tau')$ to $P$, causing $P$'s check to pass and $P$ will also output $\Hkey(g^{2xy})$. (This is not an issue if $pk$ is included in $\Htag$, since $P$ would compute $\tau = \Htag(\dots,Y^2,\dots) \neq \Htag(\dots,Y,\dots) = \tau'$ unless there is a collision in $\Htag$, and its check $\tau^* \stackrel{?}{=} \tau$ would fail.). Of course, $X^2$ can be replaced by any function of $X$ that $\adv$ can compute.

In general, $\adv$ can decrypt $(s,T)$ to recover $pk := \mathsf{2F}^{\text{-}1}(\pw,(s,T))$, then re-encrypt some $pk'$ of $\adv$'s choise under the same $\pw'$ to get $(s^*,T^*) \gets \mathsf{2F}(\pw,pk')$, and finally forward $\tau'$ but manipulate $c^*$ so that $P$'s check will pass. The ``attack'' in \Cref{app:hash-pw-pk} is the special case where $pk' = pk$; there, including $pk$ in $\Htag$ inputs forces $\adv$ not to change $pk$.

This scenario should be simulated as follows: When $\adv$ decrypts $(s,T)$ under $\pw$, $\sim$ records $\langle\pw,pk,sk\rangle$ (although there might be a large number of such decryption attempts, and $\sim$ does not know which is the ``right'' one at this point). Then when $\adv$ sends $(s^*,T^*)$ to $P'$, $\sim$ extracts $\pw$, which allows $\sim$ to retrieve the ``right'' record $\langle\pw,pk,sk\rangle$; $\sim$ also computes $K'$ while simulating the $P'$ side. Later, when $\adv$ sends $(c^*,\tau')$, $\sim$ can tell if $\adv$ is performing the aforementioned attack by checking if $\Decap(sk,c^*) = K'$.

We show the new simulator in \Cref{fig:oeke-sim-hash-pw}. (Only the steps after receiving $(c^*,\tau^*)$ are included.)

\begin{figure}[H]
\begin{framed}
\begin{small}
\underline{$P$'s session key}

\medskip
On $(c^*,\tau^*)$ from $\func$, simulate $P$'s output as follows:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item If $(s^*,T^*) = (s,T) \land (c^*,\tau^*) = (c,\tau')$, send $(\NewKey, sid, P, 0^n)$ to $\func$. \textcolor[gray]{0.5}{// $\adv$ is passive}
  {\color{blue}\item If $(s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T) \land \tau^* = \tau'$, and there has been a $(\TestPwd, sid, P, \pw')$ command to $\func$ resulting in ``correct guess'' (i.e., $\sim$ previously entered step 2(b)(ii) in \Cref{fig:oeke-sim2}), there must be a $K'$ and an $SK'$ defined at that time.
      \begin{enumerate}
        \item Retrieve record $\langle\pw',\star,sk\rangle$. If there is no such record, go to step 3. \quad \textcolor[gray]{0.5}{// $\adv$ does not decrypt $pk := \mathsf{2F}^{\text{-}1}(\pw,(s,T))$}
        \item Compute $K := \Decap(sk,c^*)$. If $K \neq K'$, go to step 3. \quad \textcolor[gray]{0.5}{// $\adv$ sends an ``incorrect'' $c^*$}
        \item Send $(\TestPwd, sid, P, \pw')$ to $\func$.
            \begin{enumerate}
              \item If $\func$ replies with ``wrong guess'', send $(\NewKey, sid, P, 0^n)$ to $\func$. \quad \textcolor[gray]{0.5}{// $P$ and $P'$'s passwords are different}
              \item If $\func$ replies with ``correct guess'', send $(\NewKey, sid, P, SK')$ to $\func$.
            \end{enumerate}
      \end{enumerate}
  }
  \item Otherwise find $\adv$'s {\color{blue}$\Htag(\pw^*,K^*)$} query resulting in $\tau^*$.
      \begin{enumerate}
        \item If there is no such query or more than one such query, send $(\TestPwd, sid, P, \bot)$ and then $(\NewKey, sid, P, 0^n)$ to $\func$.
        \item If there is exactly one such query, retrieve record $\langle\pw^*,\star,sk^*\rangle$. If there is no such record, send $(\TestPwd, sid, P, \bot)$ and then $(\NewKey, sid, P, 0^n)$ to $\func$.
        \item Compute $K := \Decap(sk^*,c^*)$. If $K^* \neq K$, send $(\TestPwd, sid, P, \bot)$ and then $(\NewKey, sid, P, 0^n)$ to $\func$.
        \item Send $(\TestPwd, sid, P, \pw^*)$ to $\func$.
            \begin{enumerate}
              \item If $\func$ replies with ``wrong guess'', send $(\NewKey, sid, P, 0^n)$ to $\func$.
              \item If $\func$ replies with ``correct guess'', compute $SK := \Hkey(K)$ and send $(\NewKey, sid, P, SK)$ to $\func$.
            \end{enumerate}
      \end{enumerate}
\end{enumerate}
\end{small}
\end{framed}
\caption{UC simulator $\sim$ for the ``hash $pk$'' variant of OEKE. Only the paragraph that needs essential change (shown in {\color{blue}blue}) is included}
\label{fig:oeke-sim-hash-pw}
\end{figure}

\subsubsection{Changes in Game Hops}
\label{app:game-hops-hash-pw}
The new security proof has a very similar structure to that in \Cref{app:game-hops-hash-pw-pk}: split Game 2 into two cases and additionally check $P'$'s $\Htag$ queries in the second case; verify that all of Games 3--16 still go through; insert new Games I and II between Game 16 and Game 17; verify that Game 17 still goes through; insert new Game III after Game 17. Below we omit Games 3--17 and only describe Game 2 and the three new games. (In fact even a large chunk of the arguments for the three new games is very similar to those in \Cref{app:game-hops-hash-pw-pk}, but we describe them in full.)

\medskip\noindent\emph{Game 2:} In the case where $\pw \neq \pw' \lor ((s^*,T^*) = (s,T) \land c^* \neq c)$, find $\adv$'s $\Htag(\pw,K^*)$ query resulting in $\tau^*$. If there is none or more than one, set $SK := \bot$. If there is a unique such query, do the following:
\begin{itemize}
  \item If $K^* = K$, set $SK := \Hkey(K)$ (i.e., there is no change from Game 1).
  \item If $K^* \neq K$, set $SK := \bot$.
\end{itemize}

Furthermore, in the case where $\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T)$, do the same as above, except that we now find $\adv$ \emph{or $P'$}'s $\Htag(\pw,K^*)$ query resulting in $\tau^*$.

The difference between the new Game 2 and the old one is that we now have two separate cases:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item $\pw \neq \pw' \lor ((s^*,T^*) = (s,T) \land c^* \neq c)$;
  \item $\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T)$.
\end{enumerate}
These two cases combined yield $\neg(\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) = (s,T) \land c^* = c)$, which is identical to the case in the old Game 2 (i.e., they cover all situations other than the one addressed in Game 1). In case (1) we proceed as in the old Game 2, whereas in case (2) we cannot due to the ``attack'' in \Cref{fig:attack-no-pk}; instead, in case (2) we need to include $P'$'s $\Htag$ query as if it were $\adv$'s.

\begin{claim}
\label{clm:htag6}
Suppose the CBIND property holds for the KEM scheme. In case (1) above, the probability that $P'$ queries $\Htag(\pw,K)$ is negligible.
\end{claim}
\begin{proof}
The proof of this claim is essentially part of the proof of \Cref{clm:htag2}. $P'$ makes a single $\Htag$ query, on $(\pw',K')$. If $\pw \neq \pw'$, then of course $P'$'s query is not $\Htag(\pw,K)$. Now assume $\pw = \pw'$. This implies $(s^*,T^*) = (s,T) \land c^* \neq c$ by the condition of the claim. Then the argument in the proof of \Cref{clm:htag2} still goes through, i.e., we can construct a reduction $\red_\text{CBIND}$ such that $\Pr[P'\text{ queries }\Htag(\pw,K)] \leq \Adv_{\red_\text{CBIND}}^\text{CBIND}$.
\end{proof}
The remaining argument is essentially identical to that in the old Game 2.

\medskip
Games 3--16 are essentially unchanged from the corresponding games in \Cref{sec:hash-pw-st}.

\medskip\noindent\emph{New Game I:} Now that $(\pw')^*$ --- the password guess extracted from $(s^*,T^*)$ --- is defined (in Game 15), we can finally add (part of) what's in step 2 of \Cref{fig:oeke-sim-hash-pw}. Concretely, we change the game as follows:

In the case where $(s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T) \land (\pw')^* = \pw = \pw' \land \tau^* = \tau'$, there is a record $\langle\pw,\star,sk\rangle$, and $\Decap(sk,c^*) = K'$, set $SK := SK'$. If $(\pw')^*$ is undefined, treat it as if $(\pw')^* \neq \pw'$. (In some sense this is the most crucial new game, as it covers the scenario in \Cref{fig:attack-no-pk} --- which is why we need to make all these changes to begin with. It also corresponds to step 2(c)(ii) in the simulator in \Cref{fig:oeke-sim-hash-pw}. We will deal with step 2(c)(i) in new Game III later.)

Since $\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T)$, Game 16 finds $\adv$ or $P'$'s $\Htag$ query resulting in $\tau^*$. $P'$ makes a singe query to $\Htag$, on input $(\pw',K')$; and the query result is $\tau' = \tau^*$. Therefore, Game 16 finds this query, and does the following:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item Check if $\pw' = \pw$, which is indeed the case.
  \item Find the $\langle\pw,\star,sk\rangle$ record.
  \item Compute $K := \Decap(sk,c^*)$ and check if $K = K'$, which is again the case per the condition of the game.
  \item Set $SK := \Hkey(K) (= \Hkey(K') = SK')$.
\end{enumerate}
This entire process in Game 16 eventually results in setting $SK := SK'$, which exactly matches the new game. Thus, there is no difference. We have
\[
\Dist_\env^{16,\text{newI}} = 0.
\]

\noindent\emph{New Game II:} In the case where $\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T)$ (i.e., case (2) in Game 2), we find $\adv$ \emph{or $P'$}'s $\Htag(\pw^*,K^*)$ query resulting in $\tau^*$ --- except that in new Game I's condition, new Game I already shortcuts it to $SK := SK'$ without trying to find any $\Htag$ query. In this game, we do not check $P'$'s $\Htag$ query anymore, and only check $\adv$'s $\Htag$ query.

There are the following cases:
\begin{itemize}
  \item If $\tau^* \neq \tau'$, then of course $P'$'s $\Htag$ query does not result in $\tau^*$ (it results in $\tau'$), so we can safely drop $P'$'s $\Htag$ query from the check.
  \item If $\tau^* = \tau'$, but there is no $\langle\pw,\star,sk\rangle$ record, then both new Game I and new Game II outright set $SK := \bot$, regardless of $\Htag$ queries by $\adv$ or $P'$. Thus, the two games are identical.
  \item If $(\pw')^* \neq \pw' \land \tau^* = \tau'$, and there is a $\langle\pw,pk,sk\rangle$ record, then $P'$'s $\Htag(\pw',K')$ query results in $\tau^*$, and we need to argue that this query can be dropped from the check.
      \begin{itemize}
        \item If $\adv$ queries $\Htag(\pw',K')$, then new Game II still finds this query, so new Game I and new Game II are identical.
        \item If $\adv$ does not query $\Htag(\pw',K')$, then new Game II sets $SK := \bot$. We argue that new Game I also sets $SK := \bot$ except with negligible probability. New Game I finds $P'$'s $\Htag(\pw',K')$ query, and sets $SK := \bot$ unless $\Decap(sk,c^*) = K'$. But $(pk,sk)$ are independent of $pk'$ by \Cref{clm:pk-ind},\footnote{\Cref{clm:pk-ind} additionally requires $c^* = c$, but its proof does not use this condition.} which suggests a reduction $\red_\text{KBIND}$ to the KBIND property of the KEM scheme: \\
            \vspace{-6pt} \\ % force \medskip in itemize environment
            \textbf{\underline{Reduction $\red_\mathrm{KBIND}$}:}
            \vspace{6pt} \\
            Sample $j \gets [q_2+1]$ as a guess that the $j$-th $H_2$ query (by either $\adv$ or $P'$) is $H_2(\pw,T^*)$. \\
            On input $(pk,pk',c,K')$,
            \begin{enumerate}
              \item Invoke $\env$. On $(\NewSession, sid, P, P', \pw, \text{``initiator''})$ from $\env$, sample $s \gets \{0,1\}^{3n}, T \gets \group$ and send $(s,T)$ to $\adv$. \\
                  When $\adv$ makes an $H_2(\pw,T) =: t$ query, compute
                  \[
                  r := s \oplus t, \quad R := T/pk.
                  \]
                  ($pk$ is part of $\red_\mathrm{KBIND}$'s input.) If $H_1(\pw,r)$ has already been defined and it is not $R$, abort. Otherwise program $H_1(\pw,r) := R$.
              \item On the $j$-th $H_2(\pw,T') =: t'$ query (by either $\adv$ or $\red_\mathrm{KBIND}$ itself on behalf of $P'$ --- see step 3 below), compute
                  \[
                  r' := s \oplus t', \quad R' := T/pk'.
                  \]
                  ($pk'$ is part of $\red_\mathrm{KBIND}$'s input.) If $H_1(\pw,r')$ has already been defined and it is not $R'$, abort. Otherwise program $H_1(\pw,r') := R'$.
              \item On $(\NewSession, sid, P', P, \pw', \text{``respondent''})$ from $\env$ and $(s^*,T^*)$ from $\adv$, if $\neg(\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T))$, abort. Otherwise
                  \begin{enumerate}
                    \item If $\adv$ has not queried $H_2(\pw,T^*)$, make this query on behalf of $P'$.
                    \item Compute $SK':= \Hkey(K')$ and $\tau' := \Htag(\pw,K')$. Output $SK'$ to $\env$, and send $(c,\tau')$ to $\adv$. ($c$ and $K'$ are part of $\red_\mathrm{KBIND}$'s input.)
                  \end{enumerate}
              \item On $(c^*,\tau^*)$ from $\adv$, if $\tau^* \neq \tau'$, abort. Otherwise output $c^*$.
            \end{enumerate}
      \end{itemize}
      Assuming $\Decap(sk,c^*) = K'$ and $\red_\text{KBIND}$'s guess of index $j$ is correct, the only difference between new Game I/II and $\red_\text{KBIND}$'s simulation (until $\adv$ sends $c^*$) is that $\red_\text{KBIND}$ uses its input $pk$ to program $H_1(\pw,r)$, uses its input $pk'$ to program $H_1(\pw',r')$, and then uses its inputs $(c,K') \gets \Encap(pk')$ as the $P'$-to-$P$ message and compute $SK'$ and $\tau'$. Since $(c,K')$ are also computed as $\Encap(pk')$ in new Game I/II, $\red_\text{KBIND}$ simulates new Game I/II perfectly. Furthermore, $\red_\text{KBIND}$ wins the KBIND game. We have
      \[
      \Pr[\Decap(sk,c^*) = K'] \leq (q_2+1)\Adv_{\red_\text{KBIND}}^\text{KBIND}.
      \]
  \item If $(\pw')^* = \pw' \land \tau^* = \tau'$, but $\Decap(sk,c^*) \neq K'$, then new Game I finds $P'$'s $\Htag(\pw',K')$ query and then sets $SK := \bot$ because the check $\Decap(sk,c^*) \stackrel{?}{=} K'$ does not pass, and new Game II also sets $SK := \bot$ because it either fails to find $\adv$'s $\Htag(\pw',K')$ query, or it finds such a query but then sets $SK := \bot$ because the check $\Decap(sk,c^*) \stackrel{?}{=} K'$ does not pass. Thus, the two games are identical.
\end{itemize}

The remaining case is that $(\pw')^* = \pw' \land \tau^* = \tau'$, there is a $\langle\pw,\star,sk\rangle$ record, and $\Decap(sk,c^*) = K'$. The condition of the game additionally requires $\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T)$. Combined, we get ``$(s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T) \land (\pw')^* = \pw = \pw' \land \tau^* = \tau'$, there is a record $\langle\pw,\star,sk\rangle$, and $\Decap(sk,c^*) = K'$''. This is exactly the condition in new Game I, in which case we do not make any change in new Game II. Overall, we conclude that
\[
\Dist_\env^{\text{newI},\text{newII}} \leq (q_2+1)\Adv_{\red_\text{KBIND}}^\text{KBIND}.
\]

Game 17 is essentially unchanged from the corresponding game in \Cref{sec:hash-pw-st}.

\medskip\noindent\emph{New Game III:}
In the case where $(s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T) \land (\pw')^* = \pw' \neq \pw \land \tau^* = \tau'$, there is a record $\langle\pw',\star,sk\rangle$, and $\Decap(sk,c^*) = K'$, set $SK := \bot$. (This corresponds to step 2(c)(i) in \Cref{fig:oeke-sim-hash-pw}.)

In this case Game 17 tries to find $\adv$'s (unique) $\Htag(\pw^*,K^*)$ query resulting in $\tau^*$, and checks if $\pw^* = \pw$ (see Game 13). But $\tau^* = \tau' = \Htag(\pw',K')$, so Game 17 sets $SK := \bot$ because it either fails to find $\adv$'s $\Htag(\pw',K')$ query, or it finds such a query but then sets $SK := \bot$ because $\pw^* = \pw' \neq \pw$. Either way, Game 17 matches new Game III which outright sets $SK := \bot$. We have
\[
\Dist_\env^{17,\text{newIII}} = 0.
\]

\paragraph{Summary.}
We have made the following essential changes to the games:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item In the case where $\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T)$ (case (2) in Game 2), Game 2 tries to find $P'$'s $\Htag$ query resulting in $\tau^*$ (in addition to $\adv$'s query).
  \item In the case where $(s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T) \land (\pw')^* = \pw = \pw' \land \tau^* = \tau'$, there is a record $\langle\pw,\star,sk\rangle$, and $\Decap(sk,c^*) = K'$, new Game I outright sets $SK := SK'$ (without trying to find any $\Htag$ query by $\adv$ or $P'$).
  \item In the case where $\pw = \pw' \land (s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T)$, new Game II drops the check on $P'$'s $\Htag$ query introduced in Game 2 (except in new Game I's condition, where all checks on $\Htag$ queries have already been dropped).
  \item In the case where $(s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T) \land (\pw')^* = \pw' \neq \pw \land \tau^* = \tau'$, there is a record $\langle\pw',\star,sk\rangle$, and $\Decap(sk,c^*) = K'$, new Game III outright sets $SK := \bot$.
\end{enumerate}

Items (1) and (3) introduce the check on $P'$'s $\Htag$ query and then drop it, so there is no net change there. To see the net change, we only need to combine items (2) and (4), which say that in the case where $(s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T) \land (\pw')^* = \pw' \land \tau^* = \tau'$, there is a record $\langle\pw',\star,sk\rangle$, and $\Decap(sk,c^*) = K'$,
\begin{itemize}
  \item If $(\pw')^* = \pw$, then we set $SK := \Hkey(K')$ [item (2)].
  \item If $(\pw')^* \neq \pw$, then we set $SK := \bot$ [item (4)].
\end{itemize}
This exactly matches step 2 of the simulator in \Cref{fig:oeke-sim-hash-pw}, so new Game III is identical to the ideal world. This completes the proof.

\paragraph{The ``hash $\pw$ and $c$'' version.}
If we define $\tau$ as $\Htag(\pw,c,K)$, then \Cref{clm:htag6} unconditionally holds, and the protocol can be proven secure under the UNPRE and KBIND properties of the KEM scheme (without the CBIND property).

\subsection{The ``Hash $pk$'' Version}
\label{app:hash-pk}
We now move on to the variant where $\pw$, but not $pk$, is further removed from $\Htag$ inputs, i.e., $\tau$ is defined as $\Htag(pk,K)$. This would best be compared with the protocol (and its security proof) in \Cref{sec:hash-pk-st}, where $\tau$ is defined as $\Htag(pk,s,T,K)$; as well as the protocol (and its security proof) in \Cref{app:hash-pw-pk}, where $\tau$ is defined as $\Htag(\pw,pk,K)$. Again there is a new scenario that requires additional care from the simulator, so we start from the changes to the simulator.

\subsubsection{Changes to the Simulator}
\label{app:hash-pk-sim}
Similar to \Cref{app:hash-pw}, once we remove $pk$ from $\Htag$, the adversary $\adv$ can force the two parties' session keys to be the same without performing a ``real'' attack. However, this time the two parties' passwords may or may not be the same (and $\adv$ needs to know both of them), and $\adv$ should forward both $c$ and $\tau'$ from $P'$ without modification. We show this scenario in \Cref{fig:attack-no-pw}.

\begin{figure}[H]
\pseudocodeblock{
P(\pw) \< \< \adv \< \< P'(\pw') \\ 
\< \sendmessageright*[1.5cm]{s,T} \< \< \< \\
\< \< pk := \mathsf{2F}^{\text{-}1}(\pw,(s,T)) \< \< \\
\< \< (s^*,T^*) \gets \mathsf{2F}(\pw',pk) \< \< \\
\< \< \<\sendmessageright*[1.5cm]{s^*,T^*} \< \\
\< \sendmessageleft*[1.5cm]{c,\tau'} \< \< \sendmessageleft*[1.5cm]{c,\tau'} \< \< \\
\text{output }SK' \< \< \< \< \text{output }SK'
}
\caption{New ``attack'' on the ``hash $pk$'' version}
\label{fig:attack-no-pw}
\end{figure}

In this ``attack'', the two parties' passwords $\pw$ and $\pw'$ may or may not be the same. (The special case where $\pw = \pw'$ is the ``attack'' in \Cref{fig:attack-no-st}.) Assuming $\adv$ knows both, it can decrypt $P$'s message to recover $pk$, and then re-encrypt $pk$ under $\pw'$; this ensures that $P'$ will recover the same $pk$ as on the $P$ side, and use it to compute $c,K',SK',\tau'$. But then if $\adv$ forwards $(c,\tau')$ without any modification, $P$ will decapsulate $c$ to the same $K'$ (because it uses the same $pk$), and its session key will be the same as $SK'$ on the $P'$ side. (This is not an issue if $\pw$ is included in $\Htag$, since forwarding $\tau' = \Htag(\pw',\dots) \neq \Htag(\pw,\dots)$ to $P$ would make $P$'s check fail unless there is a collision in $\Htag$.)

This new situation should be simulated as follows: When $\adv$ decrypts $(s,T)$ under $\pw$, the simulator $\sim$ records $\langle\pw,pk,sk\rangle$ (although there might be a large number of such decryption attempts, and $\sim$ does not know which is the ``right'' one at this point). Then when $\adv$ sends $(s^*,T^*)$ to $P'$, $\sim$ extracts $\pw'$, \emph{which also gives a $pk'$}. Later, when $\adv$ forwards $(c,\tau')$, $\sim$ knows that $\adv$ is performing the aforementioned attack, and checks which $\langle\pw,pk,sk\rangle$ record matches $pk'$. In this way $\sim$ can extract the password guess $\pw$ on the $P$ side.

We show the new simulator in \Cref{fig:oeke-sim-hash-pk}. (Only the steps after receiving $(c^*,\tau^*)$ are included.)

\begin{figure}[H]
\begin{framed}
\begin{small}
\underline{$P$'s session key}

\medskip
On $(c^*,\tau^*)$ from $\func$, simulate $P$'s output as follows:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item If $(s^*,T^*) = (s,T) \land (c^*,\tau^*) = (c,\tau')$, send $(\NewKey, sid, P', 0^n)$ to $\func$. \textcolor[gray]{0.5}{// $\adv$ is passive}
  {\color{blue}\item If $(s^*,T^*) \neq (s,T) \land (c^*,\tau^*) = (c,\tau')$, and there has been a $(\TestPwd, sid, P', \pw')$ command to $\func$ resulting in ``correct guess'' (i.e., $\sim$ previously entered step 2(b)(ii) in \Cref{fig:oeke-sim2}), there must be a $pk'$ and an $SK'$ defined at that time. 
      \begin{enumerate}
        \item Retrieve record $\langle\pw^*,pk',\star\rangle$. If there is more than one such record, abort. If there is no such record, go to step 3.
        \item Send $(\TestPwd, sid, P, \pw^*)$ to $\func$.
            \begin{enumerate}
              \item If $\func$ replies with ``wrong guess'', send $(\NewKey, sid, P, 0^n)$ to $\func$.
              \item If $\func$ replies with ``correct guess'', send $(\NewKey, sid, P, SK')$ to $\func$.
            \end{enumerate}
      \end{enumerate}
  }
  \item Otherwise find $\adv$'s {\color{blue}$\Htag(pk^*,K^*)$} query resulting in $\tau^*$.
      \begin{enumerate}
        \item If there is no such query or more than one such query, send $(\TestPwd, sid, P, \bot)$ and then $(\NewKey, sid, P, 0^n)$ to $\func$.
